### Guangdong Sets New Record in 400-Meter Relay Preliminary: —45.4 Seconds—; Shanghai Team Also Sets New Record: —45.6 Seconds— 225

(Nanjing, 14th) The 400-meter relay preliminary in the all-around competition was held in two groups.

First Group

The first group consisted of five teams: Liaoning, Ningxia, Nanjing, Gansu, and Guangdong. At the start, the Guangdong team took the lead with Zhong Lianji running the first leg. The Nanjing team was second, and the Liaoning team was third. By the fourth leg, the Liaoning team had been surpassed by the Guangdong team by more than 20 meters. Fortunately, Liu Changchun ran this leg. Mr. Liu used his swift legs to chase forward, surpassing Beijing and then chasing Guangdong. He ultimately failed by half a meter at the finish line. The Guangdong team was able to win because of their talent. Liaoning was second, and Beijing was third. The time of 45.4 seconds broke the national record. The team members were Zhong Yunjie, He Peigen, Zhu Zhongxi, and Zhao Bingheng.

Hao Chunde of Shanghai Creates the Second of Five New National Records

— Photo by Ye Changlie

Second Group

The second group consisted of four teams: Fujian, Shanghai, Beiping, and Hebei. The Shanghai team was the strongest, with Su Xiaoru running the first leg, Dong Yinchu running the second leg, Cheng Jinguan running the third leg, and Hao Chunde running the fourth leg. In the end, they surpassed the Beiping team by about 20 meters. The Hebei team was third. The time was 45 seconds.

### Many Changes Still to Come in the Decathlon: First Half Exceeds 3,000 Points; National Record Will Inevitably Be Broken; Liaoning's Liu Renxiu Abandons the Race 226

(Nanjing, 14th) Chen Baoqiu, Zhang Lingjia, Chen Ling, Liu Mengling, Zhao Enhui, and others had the best results in the first half of the decathlon. However, the conference announced the scores late on the 14th, only calculating the scores of the best performers. It is expected that there will be considerable changes in the second half. In short, the champion will be either Zhang Lingjia of Beiping or Chen Baoqiu of Shanghai. However, Liu Renxiu, who holds the national record, only attended the 100-meter event on the 14th. After running 11.8 seconds, he disappeared without a trace, giving up the race. Many people are confused. Now, the scores of Shanghai's Chen Baoqiu and Beiping's Zhang Lingjia in the first half have exceeded 3,000 points, and the national record is likely to be broken. Shanghai's Chen Ling currently has more than 2,900 points, and his scores in the javelin and pole vault will definitely be high, so there is a good chance of catching up.

### Joint Meeting of the Competition Committee and Review Committee Passes Correction of 10,000-Meter Race Results; Confirmed Error in Lap Counter's Record; Su Jinzhongkang Only Ran 19 Laps and Was Eliminated; Shanxi's Gu Desheng Takes First Place and Others Move Up Accordingly; Jiangsu Protests Yesterday, Dispute Difficult to Resolve 227

(Nanjing, 14th) At 10:00 AM on the 14th, the Competition Committee and Review Committee of the National Games held a joint meeting at the Central Hotel. Those present were Gao Zi, Ma Yuehan, Wang Zhengting, Dong Shouyi, Shen Siliang, Wu Bangwei, Zhang Xinfu, Chu Minyi, Wu Yunyu, Hao Gengsheng, Zhang Boling, and Yuan Dunli. Those attending as observers were Huang Bobin, Rong Qizhao, Li Wenchang, and Guan Songsheng. (1) The chairman reported that the judgment of the results of the men's 10,000-meter final on the 13th was based on the oral report of lap counter Huang Bobin. After reviewing the record sheets of the lap counters, the record of No. 180 (Jin Zhongkang), who was recorded as the first place in the 10,000-meter race, was only recorded by Huang Bobin and Li Wenchang. Li's record showed that No. 180 only ran 19 laps. Huang's record showed that he ran 21 laps. Running 21 laps is impossible. Therefore, there was indeed an error in Huang's record. How should it be decided? Please express your opinions. Then, lap counters Huang and Li gave separate reports. (It was generally believed that there was an error in Huang's record. Finally, Huang stated that if another person was responsible for recording the laps for No. 180, then his record could be canceled.) 1. Shen Siliang proposed accepting Li Wenchang's record as the official record. Wang Zhengting seconded the motion. The chairman called for a vote, and it passed.

Jiangsu Files Another Protest 228

According to the joint meeting of the Competition Committee and Review Committee's decision, Gu Desheng of Shanxi took first place in the 10,000-meter race, Wang Zhenglin of Shanghai took second place, Wang Huibin of Shanxi took third place, and Liu Dehua of Shandong took fourth place. The time was 34 minutes 47 and 2/5 seconds. Jin Zhongkang of Jiangsu only ran 19 laps and was eliminated. Because the track is 500 meters per lap, it is calculated as running 20 laps. After the joint meeting's records were announced at 2:00 PM on the 14th, Zhang Dongping, the head of the Jiangsu team, protested to Ma Yuehan again. The dispute over the 10,000-meter race is still difficult to resolve.

Jiangsu's Written Protest Last Night Contains Five Points 229

(Nanjing, 14th) Zhang Dongping, the head of the Jiangsu team, filed a written protest with the refereeing committee on the 14th regarding the second judgment in the 10,000-meter race, and paid a deposit of ten yuan. The original letter stated: "The resolution of the joint meeting of the Competition Committee and Review Committee, regarding the men's 10,000-meter final on the 13th, stated that there was indeed an error in the record of No. 180, who was recorded as the first place, and that Li Wenchang's record would be the official record. Now, according to Article 18 of the competition rules, this unit submits the following protest: (1) Before the start of the 10,000-meter race, there were more athletes than lap counters. After the lap counters were assigned numbers, there were still two athletes without lap counters. The finish line judge designated Huang Bobin to record No. 180, and Li Jiyuan to record another person (Fujian). Some referees witnessed this and can be called as witnesses if necessary. This proves that Huang Bobin was undoubtedly designated by the finish line judge to be responsible for counting the laps for No. 180. Why is it that after the refereeing results were announced, there was a report from Li Wenchang also recording No. 180? This is the first point of protest. (2) When the finish line judge announced that No. 180 was in first place, he stated that it was based on the evidence from the lap counter, timer, and starter. Why is it different today? This is the second point of protest. (3) The joint meeting stated that there was indeed an error in Huang's record of No. 180 running 21 laps. However, according to Huang, the number 21 on the record sheet was crossed out early with a line. How could there be 21 laps? This can be verified. This is the third point of protest. (4) During the joint meeting of the competition referee committee, Wang Zhengting stated that he did not pay attention to No. 180 in the first ten laps, but he was sure that he was closely following in the lead after the tenth lap and did not fall behind in the last two laps. Because it was dusk, he did not pay attention. Committee member Wang's moral character is admired by all, and his words are worthy of study. This is the fourth point of protest. (5) Yesterday's 10,000-meter final was closely watched by reporters from various newspapers. Each newspaper in Shanghai had detailed reports of who was leading in which lap and who took the lead in which lap. The facts were ignored, and yesterday's judgment by the finish line judge was overturned. This is the fifth point of protest. Based on the above points, regarding sporting events and refereeing ethics, we ask your committee to seriously consider and review the matter to reach a fair judgment."

Competition during the 10,000m Race

— Photo by Wang Kai

Page 18

After the 10,000m Rankings Correction, Various Parties Expressed Injustice for Jiangsu: Jin Zhongkang in First Place Extremely Obvious Fact, Said a Certain Sports Figure 232

Regarding the dispute that occurred in the 10,000m Final on the 13th, this newspaper has already published a very detailed account. However, today, a certain famous sports figure who places the utmost importance on sportsmanship told a reporter that he (this sports figure, hereinafter referred to as such) was present throughout the 10,000m Final and paid close attention to Jin Zhongkang's lap count, which was absolutely correct. Jin's championship was an extremely obvious fact. It was only after Gu Desheng of Shanxi failed to win the championship that he believed the lap counter for Jin had made a mistake. In the evening, the Shanxi representatives gathered to warn the finish line judges, Ma Yuehan, Dong Shouyi, etc., that they must overturn the record and award first place to Gu; if they did not, they would take drastic measures. Upon hearing this, the finish line judge was extremely alarmed. Northern China leaders, including Dong Shouyi and the head referee Zhang Boling, etc., secretly convened a meeting late at night to discuss how to deal with the situation. They then decided to find a way to overturn the original judgment made on the spot. During the joint meeting of the Competition Committee on the morning of the 14th, they made a powerful proposal, which was successful. Gu Desheng of Shanxi was awarded first place again, Wang Zhenglin of Shanghai was awarded second place, Wang Huibin of Shanxi was awarded third place, and Liu Dehua of Shandong was awarded fourth place. Speaking objectively, Jiangsu suffered an excessive loss. The fact is that Jin Zhongkang was first, but now Jin has no place, which is embarrassing. The finish line judges are also suspected of bias. Because they are all from Northern China, they believe that Shanxi is not easy to offend, while Jiangsu is easy to suppress. Therefore, it must be said that this is a major stain on the character of the event's referees. Although I am not from Jiangsu, I deeply feel injustice for Jiangsu, he said.

Speech by Mr. Wu Bangwei 233

According to Mr. Wu Bangwei, Jin Zhongkang's first place was an extremely obvious fact, but the finish line judge convened a meeting the next day and overturned the original decision, re-awarding Gu Desheng of Shanxi first place. This fact is strange. I do not comment on whether the referees had any bias. The Jiangsu side is willing to take a loss and does not want to engage in meaningless arguments to maintain sportsmanship.

Letter from Another Source 234

The reporter also received a letter from another source, which stated: "Today, on the 13th, a dispute occurred in the 10,000m race. One reason was that the time was too late, and the other reason was that the lap counters were arranged in a long line on both sides of the track, which was very inconvenient for the judging work. I believe that (the author of this article stated) the position of the lap counters in the first few laps does not need to be considered. In the final lap, the lap counters for the top ten or fifteen runners should stand on the track, and the other lap counters should all stand inside the inner circle of the track. After the gun is fired for the last lap, all the numbers that have passed the last lap should be reported, and the finish line judge should record them. Positions must be reserved for the timers and the finish line judges to judge the order of the runners. If the lap counters determine the order of the runners, it is inevitable that disputes like today's and those in the past will occur. I wonder what those with experience in judging think? As for today's matter, the onlookers are different and all base their opinions on their own subjective views, arguing over right and wrong. I know that the athletes must be very clear in their hearts, knowing who is beating me and where to laugh. If the athletes can come out, in accordance with the spirit of sportsmanship, and explain the true facts, it will not only eliminate the doubts of most people in this competition, but also resolve the misunderstandings of the previous Hangzhou Games. However, is there any such athlete who truly respects sportsmanship and takes action?"

Breaking the National Record in Women's Softball (Guangdong)

— Yan Xiurong (Photo by Wang Kai)

Meeting of the National Sports Federation Resolves That Membership Will Be Based on Provinces, Cities, and Special Regions; Newly Elected Directors: Wang Zhengting, Zhang Boling, Chu Minyi, Yuan Dunli, Shen Siliang, Hao Gengsheng, Gao Zi, Wu Yunrui, Ma Yuehan 235

(Nanjing, 14th) The National Sports Federation held a banquet for the representatives of various units at the Lizhi Society at 7:00 PM on the 14th, and the meeting started at 8:00 PM.

Attendees 236

The attendees were Zhang Liyan from Sichuan, Peng Zenan from Hunan, Jin Guocai from Shaanxi, Jide Liang from Beijing, Zhang Shipei from Suiyuan, Wang Jinren from Gansu, Hu Anshanji from Harbin, You Fengqi from Guizhou, Gu Yuqi from Henan, Jiang Zhujia from Shanxi, Hao Gengsheng from Qingdao, Yang Bingwen from Heilongjiang, Chen Shi from Hubei, Gong Bicheng from Xinjiang, Wu Yifeng from Anhui, Wu Bangwei from Jiangsu, Pan Gongzhan from Shanghai, Mo Yingxian, Luo Guangming from Yunnan, Chen Tang'e from the Philippines, Yuan Dunli from Beiping, Shang Shumei from Shandong, Wang Weixin, Zhao Wenzao from Hebei, Wang Zhuoran from Liaoning, Lin Pingnan from Fujian, Liu Zhu from Guangxi, Lei Hongbi from Guangdong, Yu Yongchen from Jiangxi. Also attending were Wang Zhengting, Zhang Boling, Gao Zi, Wu Yunrui, Zhang Xinfu, Jin Zhaojun, Wang Fudan, and others, totaling more than fifty people.

Chairman's Report 237

Chairman Zhang Boling, with Zhou Jiaqi as the recorder, first reported that the National Sports Federation's board of directors had been established for nine years but had not been re-elected due to the imperfect membership units, which had affected the federation's work. However, the federation's past work had made significant contributions to national sports. Due to the federation's imperfect organization, taking advantage of the opening of the National Games in Nanjing, everyone will discuss how to revise the constitution, re-elect the board of directors, etc.

Revision of the Constitution 238

Next, Wang Zhengting proposed that the domestic sports situation was different ten years ago compared to now, and the membership units were divided into sound and unsound units. He proposed revising Articles 3 and 4 of the constitution regarding membership qualifications and directors. In the end, it was resolved that (1) the members of the federation would be the provinces, cities, and special regions of the country; (2) Article 4 would be revised so that one-third of the nine directors would be re-elected every two years, and they could be re-elected consecutively; (3)

Election of New Directors 239

Wang Zhengting, Zhang Boling, Chu Minyi, Yuan Dunli, Shen Siliang, Hao Gengsheng, Gao Zi, Wu Yunrui, and Ma Yuehan were elected as the new directors; (4)

Other Motions 240

The first meeting of the board of directors will be held in Beijing on the 18th; (5) Northeastern people residing in various provinces and cities will be allowed to represent the northeastern provinces in the National Games before the lost territories are recovered.

Women's Basketball

Women's Basketball Two-Week Conclusion: Shanghai and Fujian to Meet This Morning; Fierce Rivals Will Surely Have a Dramatic Battle; Fujian Decisively Defeats Jiangxi 80 to 6; Shanghai Crushes Hunan 60 to 3; Shanghai's Momentum Is Overwhelming 241

(Nanjing, 14th Dispatch) In the second match, Shanghai versus Hunan, it was expected that the Shanghai team, renowned for its reputation, would defeat Hunan. However, Shanghai's teamwork was not as coordinated as when they were in Shanghai. Individual skills were certainly strong. After the start, Shanghai took the lead all the way. The Hunan team offered no resistance: 1-0, 4-0, soaring upwards, winning the first quarter 16-0. In the second quarter, Hunan remained the same, unable to attack or defend. Shanghai pressed forward relentlessly, feinting east and attacking west. Yang Sen played with ease, ending the first half with a score of 29-0. In the second half, the Shanghai team made significant personnel adjustments, but their momentum remained strong. Gu Xinwei hit safely, and Li Quande also scored one point. Peiping won the first inning with a score of 4-0. In the second and third innings, both sides maintained strong defenses and neither scored. In the fourth inning, Shanghai's Feng Chaoliang hit safely, and Gu Degang and Li Changfang reached first and second base due to four wild pitches. Peiping's infield set a trap. Wu Zhenbang hit a double, and Feng, Gu, and Li ran back to home base. Jin Zhendong walked, and Wu Zhenbang also returned to home base. Thus, the score was tied at 4-4. In the fifth inning, Shanghai's An Lesheng was saved by Gu Degang, and Shanghai temporarily took the lead with a score of 5-4. Peiping counterattacked. Li Guixian hit safely, and Li Quande sent Li Guixian to second and third base. The umpire mistakenly thought Li Guixian had safely ran home, and signaled to save Li Quande. Peiping took the lead again with a score of 6-5. In the sixth inning, Shanghai scored nothing. Peiping's Situ Fuxian struck out. Mao Rensheng hit a double, and Liang Ding hit safely, scoring Mao Rensheng. Li Guixian reached first base on four balls. Hu Jing hit safely, and Liang Ding scored again. The Shanghai team urgently called in veteran pitcher Wen Liandong. Li Quande struck out, and Liu Mingzan hit safely, adding another point for Li Guixian. The Shanghai team trailed with a score of 9-5. In the seventh inning, Shanghai's counterattack was ineffective, and Peiping won against Shanghai with a score of 9-5. The umpire was Hou Luoxun, and the base umpire was Le Xiurong. The scores for each inning were as follows: first inning, Shanghai 0, Peiping 4; second and third innings, both 0; fourth inning, Shanghai 4, Peiping 0; fifth inning, Shanghai 1, Peiping 2; sixth inning, Shanghai 0, Peiping 3; seventh inning, Shanghai 0, Peiping incomplete.

Old Men's Archery Competition; Zhou Jiachen First - Archery Skills Have Long Been Lost; Grand Archery Competition 280

At 9:00 AM on the 14th, the archery preliminaries began at the racecourse. Each competitor used a "Sanli" bow, with the target 30 paces away. The target consisted of a bullseye, followed by a white circle, and then a blue circle. Hitting the bullseye scored 5 points, hitting the white circle scored 3 points, and hitting the blue circle scored 1 point. Except for Xu Shixiang from Peiping, who was relatively young, the competitors were all over 40 years old, some even over 60, with white beards and missing teeth, but their spirits were still strong. It is lamentable that archery skills have been lost for decades. The results of the preliminaries are recorded below:

Shanghai's Young Ladies are Ambitious, Determined to Win the Volleyball Championship, Practicing Daily without Rest 295

The Shanghai women's volleyball team has been practicing diligently in recent days. In the preliminary round of the National Games women's volleyball competition, apart from Jiangsu and Fujian who had a bye, six matches have already concluded in sequence. The second round will begin on the 15th. The teams from Guangdong, Hong Kong, and Peiping are all formidable opponents. Shanghai will play against Fujian on the 16th, which should not pose a major problem. However, the semi-finals are just around the corner. If they are not careful, they will surely lose Jingzhou due to carelessness. Therefore, they have been intensifying their training in recent days, either mixing with the Shanghai men's volleyball team for offensive and defensive practice or playing informal matches with athletes from the Peiping team, sharpening their weapons without rest. The ambition of the Shanghai young ladies is truly gratifying for those who care about sports.

An Exciting Tennis Doubles Performance - Lin and Zheng vs. Two Generals from Batavia 296

(Nanjing, 14th Dispatch) At 10:30 AM on the 14th, Lin Saichun and Zheng Zhaojia from Sichuan and Shanghai, respectively, played a doubles exhibition match against Xu Chengji and Lin Xuyin from Batavia. All four players possessed superb skills and cooperated wonderfully, making it a rare sight. At times, they engaged in close-quarters combat, and at other times, they exchanged long shots. The situation was tense, and exciting moments were frequent. During the match, the audience gathered in large numbers, no fewer than a thousand people. Every time there was an exciting moment, applause erupted, and everyone was beaming with joy and amazed. Lin and Zheng won the first set with a score of 5-3. Xu and Lin had an absolute advantage in the second set, leading 5-2. Lin Bao, Hua, his eyes blazing, rose up in protest. Zheng Zhaojia, his spirits were high, and he stepped up his defense. The two complemented each other, winning three consecutive games and tying the score at 5-5. Then, Lin Bao, Hua served, taking the lead 6-5. But Xu and Lin also regained the serve, tying the score again at 6-6. Zheng Zhaojia's serve failed, and Lin Xuyin followed suit, making the score 7-7. Afterwards, both sides won their serves until they each had 13 games. Because it was noon and everyone was hungry, and because Zheng Zhaojia had a doubles match against Hunan in the afternoon and they were afraid of overexertion affecting the overall situation, they did not continue.

Admission Requires the Purchase of a Venue Ticket 298

(Nanjing, 14th Dispatch) The National Games swimming competition will be held on the 16th. However, the swimming pool can only accommodate 2,500 people. The organizing committee has decided that all spectators attending the swimming competition must purchase a ticket for admission. Even the president must purchase a ticket. All guest badges and long-term discount coupons are not valid. The number of tickets sold each day will be limited to the seating capacity.

Five Admission Procedures 299

(Nanjing, 14th Dispatch) The organizing committee announced five admission procedures for the swimming pool: (1) All members of the organizing committee, athletes from various units, other athletes, and all guests, except for swimming referees and swimming instructors, must purchase a ticket for admission. However, the number of daily tickets is limited to 2,500. Each ticket is priced at 5 jiao and is limited to one person. (2) Each newspaper will be given one press pass per day, movie cameramen will be given ten passes per day, China Publicity Society cameramen will be given six passes, Wang Kai cameramen will be given six passes, and broadcasters will be given two passes. Each pass is limited to one person. The above passes will be distributed by the organizing committee's publicity team. (3) Swimming referees, swimming athletes, swimming instructors, cameramen, and broadcasters will enter the venue through the main entrance of the swimming pool. (4) Spectators will enter the venue through the east and west side doors of the swimming pool. (5) Journalists will enter the venue through the back door of the swimming pool.

A Strange Person Found Behind the Temporary Market Yesterday; A Shandong Jinan Native, a Student Studying in France, Was Robbed on the Way and Ended Up in Nanjing; Suddenly Disappeared After a Full Meal 300

(Nanjing, 15th Dispatch) Yesterday, a strange person was found lying on the grass behind the temporary market at the sports meet, wearing an old Western suit and underwear, groaning. His eyes were strangely red, as if he were very tired. After being questioned by the police, he claimed to be Guo Xinghai, 24 years old, from Jinan Prefecture, Shandong, a student studying in France. His luggage was stolen on the way from Hong Kong to Shanghai, which led to his being stranded here. The day before, he had been sleeping in the Mausoleum Enclosure, and the next evening, he was lying here, very hungry. After he was given a full meal, the crowd notified the Shandong representatives to provide him with information and investigate whether he was a student studying in France. They invited someone who knew French to converse with him, and he spoke fluently. They asked him to have a full meal and inquired about his family situation, preparing to send him back home or to have him return to his hometown with the team members. Seeing the gifts given to him, Guo said that he only wanted to eat, and he did not talk about the others. The Shandong team praised his ambition, but Guo suddenly left the team and disappeared.

Harbin Women's Basketball Team

Anecdotes from the Venue 306

On the fourth day of the National Games, the weather was clear and the breeze was gentle. In addition, the various athletics events were finals, which aroused great interest. Therefore, spectators came in droves. The seats in the athletics field were almost full, and there was no room to stand on the east and west grandstands.

Zeng Zhongming Hustles to Take Pictures 307

Zeng Zhongming, the Vice Minister of the Railways, brought his own camera. After 2 PM, he went to the athletics field and ascended the grandstand to watch the events. Ms. Xu Lai was also there, and they exchanged brief pleasantries. Zeng then hurriedly went down the grandstand and entered the athletics field to take pictures of the athletes. Sun Ke arrived with his wife and daughters, and Zeng took pictures of them on the track. Soon after, Gu Mengyu also arrived with fashionable female companions, and Zeng rushed to greet them and take pictures as well, extremely busy. It was said that Vice Minister Zeng was serving Wang Kai, very motivated.

200-Meter Finals Moved 308

The 200-meter finals, held in the afternoon, generated high interest because of Liu Changchun's reputation and the expectation of a new record. However, the track and field authorities suddenly decided to move the race to the track in front of the east grandstand. The reason given was that the west track was uneven due to continuous running and trampling, which might hinder the breaking of a new record. Therefore, the race was moved from west to east, with no other intention. However, the reporters, numbering over a hundred, assumed that the move was because many important people were on the east grandstand, so they were ordered to move east. They gathered and stormed through the athletics field, heading straight for the east grandstand. The Boy Scouts initially refused to let them pass, saying they had not received orders. However, the crowd rushed in, and they could do nothing. Zhou Xiangxian, a member of the organizing committee, saw the situation and asked about it in a tactful manner. After learning the inside story, everyone laughed.

"Women's Army" Disappointed 309

During the women's softball game on the morning of the 13th, several male athletes ran into the athletics field at the entrance of the west grandstand. The female Boy Scouts on guard tried to stop them, but they were overwhelmed and only managed to stop one person, trying to force him out. However, the male athlete pretended to leave and suddenly ran back into the field. The female Boy Scout, unaware, quickly turned around and chased after him. But the male athlete had been trained to have swift feet, and the female Boy Scout could not catch up. After chasing for about fifty meters, she returned in defeat. Those who saw it burst into laughter, saying that the female Boy Scout was acting as a "spotter". The "women's army", their faces red with embarrassment, left the field, angry and not knowing where to go.

Controversy Caused by the Golden Lance 310

The golden lance given by President Lin Sen as a prize was moved to the entrance in front of the west grandstand for photography, and the arrangement was very exquisite, worthy of its fame. Xu Yanzhi, the director of the prize department, stretched out both hands to block pedestrians to prevent them from obstructing the lens. Unexpectedly, the audience was rushing to watch the 200-meter finals, and they rushed into the venue. The director of the organizing committee was also at the entrance to maintain order. A Boy Scout commander saw the situation and rushed to the entrance to assist. Unexpectedly, Xu placed his hands on the Boy Scout commander's hands and pushed them away, regardless of everything, heading straight for the entrance. Xu was the director of the prize department, and the photography of the golden lance given by President Lin, a senior government official, was important. He glared at the Boy Scout commander, blaming him for being uncooperative. The Boy Scout commander, claiming the righteousness of maintaining order, blamed Xu in return. They argued fiercely, and Zhang Xinfu and others mediated the situation. However, one wave subsided, and another rose, arousing the anger of another Boy Scout leader. He angrily said to Zhang Xinfu, "The organizing committee is handling things like this, holding the Boy Scouts responsible. What kind of system is this? If the organizing committee cannot take responsibility, then our Boy Scouts will all withdraw!" Zhang tried his best to smooth things over, expressing goodwill, and the Boy Scout's anger subsided slightly.

China's First "Industrious Sports Monthly" is Selling Well 311

The "Industrious Sports Monthly," published by the Industrious Bookstore at 392 Rue Pére Robert, French Concession, this city, in response to the trends of the times and the needs of the national sports community, and edited by sports expert Zhao Rugan, etc., is rich in content and well-made, and has won the praise of the sports community. The first issue, published on the 10th of this month, with its eight-page "Book News" section, is the most famous. The "Words and Opinions" and "Commentary" sections contain the carefully crafted works of sixteen experts, including Bu Ma Chonggan, Shao Rugan, Jiang Xiangqing, Liu Shenzhan, Yu Binqi, Wu Yunrui, Hao Gengsheng, Shen Siliang, Shang Shuzhi, Liu Xuesong, Chen Baiqing, Wang Fudan, Sun Hebao, Lu Xiangqian, and Wu Tu Liang and Ruan Weicun. The "Teaching Materials" section contains various teaching materials from five experts, including Cheng Dengke, Wang Geng, Ruan Weicun, Shao Rugan, and Hu Jingxi. The materials are not only novel in their themes but also highly practical. There is also a six-section "Sports News" section, with detailed and interesting descriptions of the successes of male and female athletes, important national sports news, and local sports news. The entire book contains 100,000 words in a large volume, and each copy is priced at 2 jiao, with a full year (10 issues) costing 2 jiao and 4 fen. Domestic postage is 2 jiao and 4 fen, and foreign postage is 1 yuan and 8 jiao. A full-year subscription is only 1 yuan and 2 jiao, with no domestic postage charged, until the end of this month. The bureau, in order to promote sports nationwide, is not afraid of sacrifice. On the previous day (the 10th), it specially transported 6,000 copies of the first issue to Beijing to be distributed to the National Games staff to promote the event. Recently, orders and subscriptions have been pouring in to the bureau's distribution office, the retail department at 554 Fourth Road, and the temporary shop at the Nanjing Games venue. Newspaper vendors in this city are also selling the magazine.

Establishment of the Northwest Seven Provinces Physical Education Promotion Association; Northwest Games to be Held in Gansu Next Year; Promoting Physical Education Progress and Cultivating Benevolence and Chivalrous Virtues 312

Ningxia Correspondence: Physical education in the Northwest provinces has always been known to be backward. The Ningxia Provincial Department of Education, after the closing of the first Northwest Games, specially convened a meeting of representatives of various provinces in Ningxia to establish the Northwest Physical Education Promotion Association. Wang Dehou and Wu Jinzhou from Gansu, Hao Renzhong from Shanxi, Ma Shirong from Qinghai, and Jin Luhe from Ningxia attended. They passed the charter of the Promotion Association and resolved that the Northwest Games next year will be held in Gansu Province. The main points of the charter are excerpted as follows: (Organization) The association will be temporarily organized by representatives from the seven provinces of Gansu, Ningxia, Qinghai, Shaanxi, Suiyuan, Xinjiang, and Shanxi. (Purpose) (1) To promote the progress of physical education in the Northwest provinces and prepare for participation in the National Games. (2) To unite physical educators in the Northwest provinces, develop a spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation, and cultivate the virtues of benevolence and chivalry. (3) To formulate and implement an overall plan for the development of physical education in the Northwest. (Location) The association's address will be located in the provincial government or Department of Education of the province where the next Northwest Games are held. (Meetings) (1) Regular Meeting: The regular meeting of the association will be held one day after the opening of the games in the host province, with two representatives from each province. However, the attendance of representatives from more than half of the units (provinces) is required. In case of special circumstances, the host province of the games may convene a meeting temporarily by letter or telegram. (3) Games: The participating provinces shall take turns holding the games every autumn (spring). (Rights) Each province shall have one voting right. (Athlete Qualifications) The provisions of the amateur sports rules of the National Physical Education Promotion Association shall be followed. (Sports Events and Methods) All shall be based on the latest regulations of the National Games.

Shanghai Municipal Education Association Council Meeting; Re-discussing the Central Government's Unified Management of the Boxer Indemnity; Establishing Sixteen People's Schools in Various Factory Areas 313

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association held its sixth temporary council meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday. Huang Zaoxiong, Chen Jicheng, Zhou Feicheng, Ma Jiazhen, Xu Zeyi, and Hao Naiding attended. Zhou Feicheng presided over the meeting, and Zhang Libai served as the recorder. Matters discussed: (1) The proposal of the Second District Education Association requesting a monthly subsidy was resolved to follow up on the previous proposal. (2) The letter from the Eighth District Education Association requesting the purchase of Xu Zhengji's Practical Abacus Study as the abacus textbook for people's schools was resolved to assign Councilor Hao Naiding to review the book and Councilor Huang Zaoxiong to review the expenses for people's school supplies, and to handle the matter appropriately after the reviews are completed. (3) The proposal to request the Municipal Education Bureau to allocate the vacated buildings after the Municipal Education Bureau's relocation to the association as its headquarters was resolved to be passed and submitted to the Municipal Education Bureau. (4) Regarding the association's previous resolution on unified management measures for the Boxer Indemnity, public announcement of income and expenditure, and the establishment of the China International Library, the proposal to resubmit to the Executive Yuan and the Central Executive Committee after they were not approved was resolved to be passed and resubmitted to the Central Executive Committee. (5) Councilors Zhang Zhongdao and Huang Zaoxiong proposed to appoint Sheng Chunan as the principal of a people's school, Councilor Ma Jiazhen proposed to appoint Hu Zu'en as the principal of a people's school, Councilor Xu Zeyi proposed to appoint Liu Yingshun as the principal of a people's school, Councilor Tao Baichuan proposed to appoint Li Shihui, Huang Weibang, and Wu Rusheng as the principals of people's schools, and various factory areas requested the establishment of people's schools. It was resolved to appoint Hu Zu'en as the principal of the Seventh People's School, Xu Zhiji as the principal of the Eighth People's School, Sheng Chunan as the principal of the Ninth People's School, Li Shihui as the principal of the First People's School, Huang Weibang as the principal of the Eleventh People's School, Wu Rusheng as the principal of the Second People's School, Jiang Han as the principal of the Thirteenth People's School, Zhang Lichun as the principal of the Fourteenth People's School, Huang Kewu as the principal of the Fifteenth People's School, Liu Yingshun as the principal of the Sixteenth People's School, and Liu Linyuan as the principal of the Seventeenth People's School. The expenses for the Seventh, Eighth, and Sixteenth People's Schools shall be handled appropriately according to the Fifth People's School method. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Spring and Autumn

Special Edition Night Scenery A Sketch of the Night 315

— Qiu Yun

Various objects, more meaningful than in the daytime, dance in people's minds! The flashing original forms of red and green electric lights seem to be offering coquettish glances to all the elders!

Red and green, the softly swaying lines on the dance floor gently entangle a skinny bone on the ground.

In the halls of Western-style buildings, what crawls out of the windows are also some lights, a few shadows, also red and green, and also sounds: unrestrained laughter, beautiful singing, rhythmic piano sounds.

And from who knows where, with indistinct directions and untraceable origins, it seems that everything around is echoing each other: this kind of mixed and clamorous shouting!

In restaurants, the constant ringing of telephones, and beside the telephones, many young girls' hearts are beating and trembling!

Vehicles: cars, trams, motorcycles, like many crazy fellows, running and shouting!

Far and near, steamships roar!

The night has no moon, and the sky is patched with layers of dark clouds, densely covering it! But from a distance, it is a red sky!

Night on Nanjing Road 316

— Yu Renwei

The night on Nanjing Road is truly magnificent! Standing below Sassoon House and looking westward, one sees red neon lights shining like daylight, illuminating a tarred road, covering the ground in red; the magnificent buildings are all reflected beneath people's feet; the streetcars rushing back and forth, dashing and disappearing like flying.

The uplifting music inside the Cathay Hotel blows with the wind into people's eardrums; people on the street outside can see Western men and women inside, holding silver cups and casually sipping wine and Holland water. The small-time fellows who lack such fortune stare with lantern-like eye sockets, swallowing saliva in their mouths.

In front of the Huamao Hotel's window, two Western women are viewing various clothing samples. An old hustler, holding a copper watch in his hand, waves it back and forth in front of them in a thief-like manner, leaving the two Western women bewildered, mumbling something in their mouths.

A boy who looks like a houseboy, holding a stack of letters, stuffs them all into a mailbox in front of the Huilo Company, and in a flash, darts across the road like a flying arrow.

In front of the Wing On Company, a few prostitutes standing there suddenly become restless and start pulling customers. The one being pulled says in a low voice, "It's still early!"

Ah! Our Nanjing Road! You are magnificent, you are mysterious, you make people drunk, you make people linger unwilling to leave you.

Night on the Street of Mystery 317

— Uncle Xun

The brilliant streetlights shoot straight into the clouds, patches of red glow reflecting in the deep gray floating clouds; the twilight only gradually thickens, followed by the night sounds sadly groaning in the sky, as if telling people, "The god of night has descended upon the world, and the drama of all evils is about to begin."

Indeed, this drama of evil is performed most intensely on North Sichuan Road, known as the Street of Mystery. When I and Ying Jun were pacing on the wide Sichuan Road Bridge, the clock of the General Post Office had already struck eight times, the cars, rickshaws, and carriages were emitting various rhythms, the red lights and streetlights were flashing in the crossroads in a variety of patterns, and the pedestrians were exceptionally crowded, walking back and forth.

On the sidewalks on both sides, in the crowds, stood countless young girls selling their souls, waiting, waiting, occasionally emitting a miserable guttural sound! Extending thin white hands, dragging and pulling at passersby.

Clearly: Judging from this situation, North Sichuan Road has completely transformed from decline to bustling. Here! There are no broken tiles from bombings. Here! There are no knife-stabbed cracks, but here! There are only tall Western-style buildings and luxurious cinemas and restaurants.

On the road; there is the sound of Japanese women's wooden clogs! There is also the drunken roaring of English sailors: and even the jazz sounds playing waltzes and Charleston tunes... humming: spreading from this Street of Mystery, composing the symphony of the night.

The wind blows, blowing all over this snake-like North Sichuan Road.

Suzhou at Night 318

— Zhu Gui

Night in Suzhou is not as mysterious and lively as in Shanghai. Although when the curtain of night unfolds, in the center of the city—Guanqian Street—there are also red and green neon lights, emitting dazzling light, and in the Lei Dianhua, singing soul-stirring songs, snake-like women, in the streets and on the sidewalks, twisting out graceful postures; those white and slightly dark fleshy legs, even more greasily, under the long-slit cheongsams, emit a tempting flesh color. If it is in the summer.

But after nine o'clock, the stores on Guanqian Street gradually close, with only a few food stores and cigarette stores remaining sparsely, the lights are gradually dimmed, the pedestrians are gradually sparse, only the remaining shop assistants in the few open shops, and the policemen standing guard on the street, are still struggling to stay awake; the rickshaw pullers in the street are also dozing off while sitting on the parked rickshaws. - Although there are a few restaurants, from time to time flying out the sounds of drinking games.

After ten o'clock, the cinemas also end their shows, although there is still a Peking opera house, performing its best show with gongs and drums in full swing; however, except for a few dim sum shops nearby, still waiting for theatergoers after the show, the stores have all closed their doors. As for people, except for newspaper reporters, guards, and some workers, there are only a few wonton vendors and tea egg sellers, hissing in the cold wind. Even the rickshaw pullers lined up outside the theater are dozing off, waiting for the theater to close and do one last business - outside Jinmen Gate, it is indeed a bit more lively. Those young girls, maids, and other street ladies, like flower butterflies, shuttle in and out of the hotels, and the "Little Easterner...", "Slaves come to play the huqin..." Peking opera tunes and ditties, from time to time, along with the clear huqin sounds, spread from the hotel rooms or restaurants, making the road exceptionally lively, with policemen on duty, patrols checking the streets, pimps soliciting customers, street-wandering hooligans, fortunetellers on the sidewalks... As for the shops, except for teahouses, nine out of ten are still open, until the Peking opera ends in the middle of the night.

The singing girls in Minqing Lane, under the protection of the Minzu Society, have long since resumed the prostitute life of the "Changsan" type, with drinking parties and card games in the courtyard still in full swing until late at night. The chartered cars with electric lights are the only colorful objects on the road in Suzhou at night.

This is the "Night in Suzhou," the paradise on earth!

West Lake at Night 319

— Yang Yi

One day, perhaps it was exactly June 16th of the lunar calendar, I strolled to Pinghu Qiuyue, one of the famous scenic spots on Bai Causeway in West Lake, to cool off in the evening.

That dreadful sun had just been swallowed by the short, elegant peaks. The surrounding hazy green mountains, near and far, gradually lost their beautiful appearance; they seemed to be getting sick, changing from pale white to a terrible iron-green face. The clear green lake water also turned black.

Pairs of male and female tourists, young students, walked along Bai Causeway and the road, under the weeping willows and electric lights, talking, laughing, and playing. The small boats on the lake, carrying old men, old women, children, girls, students, and lovers, competed to row with great strides. On the lakeside road and Bai Causeway, the cars of wealthy people raced roaringly.

Music, opera singing, laughter, noise, dog barks, insect sounds, frog sounds, wind sounds, water sounds, children's crying, and the sounds of bells and drums from mountain temples all came from various places far and near, overwhelming the senses.

"Good! Beautiful!"

"Look! Isn't that a fireball!"

"It's as red as blood!"

"Look! How beautiful! Isn't that a fire dragon on the lake!"

Suddenly a burst of shouts. The children jumped and shouted excitedly.

The teary stars seemed to be preparing to welcome the moon.

At this time, feeling too noisy, I left Pinghu Qiuyue and walked along Bai Causeway towards the already very perfect Broken Bridge. The Baochu Pagoda, towering on Geling Hill, silently overlooked the calm lake. In the inner West Lake, the red, white, and pink lotuses, and the green silk umbrella-like lotus leaves, which competed for beauty during the day, now seemed to be lazily swaying in the breeze and sleeping silently because they could not show their beauty.

Looking back at the bright moon that was striving to rise, it seemed to smile at the tourists on the lake and say:

Don't be too lazy!

Don't be greedy for play!

Don't lose the great and precious time!

Come on!

Come! Follow me and keep moving forward without stopping!

Night's Seller of Smiles 320

— Jin Lou

Late at night, I tread forward on the silver streets of the city. The arc lights of the colorful stores give people a strong pink stimulation, and in the surrounding shadows stand chicken prostitutes selling their flesh piecemeal. I cannot bear to look at their bright red colors, and I quickly escape!

In my ears are the noisy singing sounds. The Eastern Hotel, lying like a corpse, is brightly lit by white-hot electric lights. On the curtains: the shadows of people and the light of cups are still intertwined, and bursts of laughter still pour out. This laughter seems to be the gnawing laughter of people with blood seeping from their teeth!

I am a little angry and begin to curse:

These, these who are active in piles of gold, these who are lost in gold-selling dens, these who endlessly taste the flavor of flesh in pink dreams... Ah! Who says it is not an extreme mockery of our decadent souls? Who says it is not an extreme persecution of those sellers of smiles who expose their flesh for the sake of life's squeezing?

I do not curse the wax-like singing girls under the strong lights. Perhaps they are not entirely seeking the gifts of gold. They are all memorable sellers of smiles of the night who have been destroyed by the whip of life, but their smiles, what have they ever been smiles? Their songs, what have they ever been songs? They are the trembling cries, weak, small, and withered! They cry out the sorrows of all weak souls and all those whose hearts have been insulted;

They—the sellers of smiles of the night—can never obtain a safe life, and never dare to give up blood-seeping greasepaint and tear-swallowing seductive smiles. They are always being persecuted in the shadows of the night, under the baking of the hot lights—until they die!

Thus, pitifully! These sellers of smiles of the night, who have no real understanding and resistance, are also always pitied under our pen tips!

"Ah! Sellers of smiles of the night!

You are the female convicts violated by brutal soldiers in the Siberian penal colony!

You are the female followers who are forced to expose their flesh in the marketplace in Jerusalem by the Jews!"

Miscellaneous Notes

Night University Hodgepodge 321

— Huang Yingdai

This is truly full of wonders. In the metropolis of Shanghai, in addition to ordinary universities, there are also night universities. As the name suggests, night universities naturally have classes in the evening. Because classes are held in the evening, life here is different from that of ordinary universities.

In an era when university tuition is so expensive, if your family has no property, don't even think about crossing the threshold. A son studying at a university must have his family send eight hundred to a thousand dollars a year. However, in night universities, everyone has a job during the day and feels that their knowledge is not enough, so they use their spare time at night to study at night universities. Therefore, there is obviously a manifestation of populism here, and there is no need for families to send money.

Classes start at 4:30, but the office must close at 5:00. This class really can't be chosen! Even if you choose a 5:30 class, running from the office to the school at 5:00 is not enough time if the road is far. At this time, most of the students are running in a hurry, even more urgently than soldiers going to the front line, afraid of missing the start of class, and when they arrive at school, they are already out of breath.

Working during the day and studying at night is already implementing a work-study model, providing for one's own tuition and integrating occupation and education, which is a proud thing. But after working seven or eight hours during the day and then studying for four or five hours at night, energy is limited. In the classroom, if the teacher can't lift the students' spirits, many people may fall asleep!

Although there are young men in suits and fashionable ladies studying knowledge in the same classroom, there is no competition for queen or the title of princess here. Female students and male students rarely talk to each other, except for a very few; therefore, if you encounter male and female students talking together, it will attract a lot of attention, so-called rare and strange!

If you choose three or four hours of classes continuously from 4:30 to 9:30, eating dinner becomes a problem. Listening to lectures on an empty stomach, with ears and hands working hard, while the stomach is singing its empty city strategy, this is a special flavor. By the time class is over, it is already ravenously hungry, and there is no time to go home to eat.

Although in this night university, there is a manifestation of a populist color, most of the students walk to and from school, but there are also a few cars picking up and dropping off students, but it is only a minority; therefore, when school is dismissed, they in their cars will attract the attention and envy of the general students.

When school is dismissed, male and female students go down the narrow escalator, walk out the door, and disperse to go home. Occasionally, a male student will follow a female student, intentionally or unintentionally, I don't care, but we rarely see them turn around. Here, the fact is clearly telling us that the female students in night university all express an attitude of "sacred and inviolable"!

Free Talk

On Building New Villages 322

— Tang Tao

In recent years, affected by social instability, people have wanted to escape reality. Those who advocate suicide think that once is enough, and those who convert to Buddhism always see everything as flowers in a mirror and the moon in the water. Even if it is not completely unconscious, the result of self-perfection not only does not remedy the instability but only indirectly helps it grow.

In this negative situation, it is gratifying that a group that strives to build new villages has emerged.

Since the May Fourth Movement, the organization of the old society has no longer been suitable for general needs. The literary and artistic circles hold their initial ideals and spare no effort in advocating the construction of new villages. Such ideals have also been frequently expressed in novels. In recent years, many intellectuals who have returned from overseas, have been to the villages of emerging countries, and have lived a fresh and lively life, once they return to this environment that has not easily changed for two thousand years, the dryness and noise drive them to embark on the road of reform; under hasty management, the plan for the new village is put into practice.

However, following this practice, it is still a piece of dryness and noise. They failed.

The reasons for the failure, in addition to the fact that China's politics are not on track, always giving social reformers great pain, the second reason is the imperfection of the internal organization.

Later comers have no reason to repeat this mistake.

Everyone knows that what can be built in the hearts of the masses is a sound cause. And today's Chinese masses are the toiling poor. The first step that urgently needs to be transformed is the life of the small rooms, attics, thatched sheds, and huts. Building new villages should start with this class. As for the petty bourgeoisie who own tens of thousands of dollars in cash, although they can build a few new Western-style houses and form a new village, how long will it be before everything has to decline with their souls?

Moreover, the plan for the new village is not an escape, and there can be no slightest illusion of Utopia. The life of the residents of the new village should not be a life of leisure and enjoyment, but a life of more actively fighting with life in the same goal and under the same pace.

All slogans of comfort and beauty are superfluous here.

Saneatsu Mushanokōji said it well: "The purpose of the new village is to manage people's lives, walk the right path of people, solve the worries of clothing, food, and shelter, promote the glory of people, and establish faith in people." (Only from what I can remember). The "people" referred to here have a correct and new meaning.

Therefore, the responsibility of the new village is to ensure that there is no inhuman life, inhuman behavior, and inhuman thought in this world; the responsibility of the new village is to advance, not to retreat.

After "Recollections of the Past" (Part 1) 323

— Feng Zhiyu

I wasn't careful and indulged in a bit of reminiscing, which drew out an article from Mr. Shi Zhecun, "Zhuangzi and Selections of Refined Literature," who thought that my words were aimed at him, yet hoped they weren't.

I would like to make a few clarifications: that "Recollections of the Past" was not written for Mr. Shi, but it could include him.

If I were targeting someone specifically, according to modern writing conventions, I should have investigated the opponent's place of origin, background, appearance, and even what products their hometown produces and what kind of shop their father owned, and subtly insult them a few times to be considered proper. But my piece contained none of these things. What I was referring to was the general atmosphere of a large group of remnants of the past; I wasn't singling out anyone in particular. But because I was referring to a group, it was inevitable that many would feel touched, even if not entirely, at least a part of them, even if they don't always belong to that group, they sometimes do. Now, Mr. Shi himself said that he advised young people to read "Zhuangzi and Selections of Refined Literature" "to help with literary cultivation," which naturally has some relevance to what I was criticizing. But to think that this article was written for him is truly "nervous oversensitivity." I really didn't mean that.

However, that was before Mr. Shi explained his views. Now, even that "relevance" feels a bit distant because what I was criticizing was a more stubborn group of remnants of the past with even higher standards.

Now, after reading Mr. Shi's own explanation: (1) I realized that his situation at the time was because the manuscript paper was too small, and "if it had been a bit wider," he "wanted to write several more books in it." (2) I realized that his previous experience was "switching from a Chinese teacher to editing a magazine," and he felt that "young people's writing was too clumsy and straightforward, and their vocabulary was too limited," so he recommended these two ancient books to have them learn grammar and find vocabulary, "even though many of the words in them are dead." I think if Zhuangzi were alive today, after having his coffin split open, he would probably advise all women who aspire to marriage to read "Biographies of Exemplary Women."

Here's another point:

(1) Mr. Shi said that I used bottles and wine to compare to "literary cultivation," which is incorrect. I never made such a comparison. I said that some new youths can have old ideas, and some old forms can contain new content. I also believe that there cannot be a clear division between "new literature" and "old literature," but there is transformation and a comparative bias. And precisely because there can be no "definitive division," there is no "third type of person's" standpoint.

(2) Mr. Shi said that writing rare characters and the like is a personal matter, as long as you don't force others to do the same. This seems very reasonable. However, middle school students and contributors, it is their own writing which is too clumsy and straightforward, and their vocabulary which is too small. They haven't forced others to write articles with limited vocabulary and clumsy grammar. Why did Mr. Shi feel so deeply and therefore advise "young people aspiring to literature" to read "Zhuangzi and Selections of Refined Literature"? When he was an examiner, selecting scholars based on wording, Mr. Shi didn't agree with that, but as a teacher and editor, he advised young people to read "Zhuangzi and Selections of Refined Literature." I really don't understand what the distinction is between these situations.

(3) Mr. Shi even brought up "Mr. Lu Xun," as if he inherited the new orthodox tradition of "Zhuangzi" and all of his articles were written after reading "Zhuangzi and Selections of Refined Literature." "I think this is also a bit arbitrary." In his articles, there are indeed many words that are found in "Zhuangzi and Selections of Refined Literature," such as "zhi, hu, zhe, ye," but these words are probably also found in other books. To put it bluntly, looking for living vocabulary from such books is simply foolish. I'm afraid Mr. Shi himself might not even do that.

Brief Notes on Autumnal Shade: On Buying Books 324

— Yu Dafu

Two or three years ago, Holbrook Jackson in England published a major work, Anatomy of Biblionlania. This "Anatomy of a Book Maniac" is rich in content and comprehensive in its citations. It can truly be compared to Robert Burton's Anatomy of Melancholy. The psychology of book maniacs, both ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign, seems to be the same. China has research on Song edition butterfly bindings, Ming printed cotton paper, etc. Foreign collectors are also willing to spend tens of thousands of gold yuan to buy a first edition of a collection of poems or essays. For example, the collection of poems by the Brontë sisters, published by Aylott and Jones, a thin volume Poems by Currer, Ellis, and Acton Bell can sell for eight or nine hundred pounds or more. The reason is that one day Charlotte suddenly discovered Emily's poetry manuscript, and the three sisters discussed publishing a collection of poems at their own expense. Fortunately, Aylott & Jones, a publisher in London, agreed to print and publish it for them for thirty pounds. But after a year, only two copies of this collection of poems were sold. The three sisters, after sending a few copies to friends, decided to sell the rest of the poems to a paper shop to be used as lining. But later, they transferred it to Smith, Elder & Co. under better conditions for publication, so the collection of poems printed by Aylott & Jones can sell for such a high price.

This kind of increase in the market value of rare books also became popular in China after Hu Shi wrote several textual researches on novels. Now, even elementary textbooks such as the Three Character Classic, Hundred Family Surnames, and Dragon Text Shadow, printed on yellow paper in this version, sell for several dollars a copy. So-called Sinology has become the exclusive knowledge of the rich. The poor are left to learn the ABCs to seek shortcuts. Thus, the cunning old booksellers who hoard books get their way, and everyone is getting rich.

A few months ago, Mr. Shi Zhecun wrote an article about buying Western old books in Shanghai, but based on my own experience, the prices of Western old books in Shanghai are also not cheap. Whenever I see a beloved old book and can't negotiate a price, I really have the urge to invite Hitler or Qin Shi Huang to implement dictatorship. But when I walk to the street and think calmly, there are still tens of millions of Chinese compatriots starving and freezing, waiting to die. Then I feel that our buying books is the same kind of vice as the capitalists' wild revelry.

Chen Jiongming and the Zhi Gong Tang 325

— He Ru

It was reported in the newspaper a month ago that Chen Jiongming's spirit hall had a Zhi Gong Tang party flag covering his coffin, indicating that he was the leader of the Zhi Gong Tang. The flag has the shape of a "bing" character, symbolizing the well-field system to indicate the meaning of equalizing land rights, and that those who till the land should own it. What is the Zhi Gong Tang or Zhi Gong Party? Not many people know. Here, according to the Tongmenghui's organ magazine, Min Bao, I will briefly describe it.

The gist of the Zhi Yi Tang's revised charter states: "The establishment of the Zhi Gong Tang has a long history. Based on the heart of loving the country and protecting the race, we establish the ambition of reviving the Han and avenging wrongs. We form alliances and gather together, responding to each other's calls. Nationalistic thought relies on it to flourish, and secret societies grow day by day because of it. It has long been spread throughout the eighteen provinces and the countries of the five continents. Wherever Chinese people go, there is one, especially in America. Residing in a region of equality and freedom, and in a nation of benevolent governance, forming alliances and unions are all unrestricted. Therefore, the development of the Hongmen is only natural." It can be seen that the Zhi Gong Tang was originally a secret society of the Hongmen, with national revolutionary ideas, originating in China and developing in the United States. It is said that at that time, the number of overseas Chinese students in the United States who were members of the Zhi Gong Tang was in the tens of thousands, which gives an idea of its prosperity. Its revised charter also states: "Now, fortunately, we have met the patriotic person, Mr. Sun Yat-sen, who has come to travel to the Americas. This Tang invited Huang Sande and other elders to travel to various ports, speaking on the tenets of the Hongmen and expounding on current Chinese affairs. Comrades in various ports began to awaken as if from a great dream, and realized that our party has a responsibility for the future of China. Mr. Sun further revised the charter, providing guidance, so that our overseas Chinese compatriots can rise up with the times." This can be used to examine the initial combination of the Nationalist Party and the Zhi Gong Tang, and Sun Yat-sen was the initiator of the Tang's reform. Writers of revolutionary history should not be unaware of this. Its revised charter outlines the following:

This Tang takes expelling the Manchus, restoring China, establishing the Republic, and equalizing land rights as its tenets.

This Tang takes cooperating to assist comrades in the motherland in implementing the tenets as its goal. All new members must abide by the teachings of Hongmen incense master Chen Jinnan, and observe the rites of entry.

Looking at its outline, it already has the scale of a revolutionary party, and Mr. Sun Yat-sen "revised the charter, providing guidance," and actually led it. After Chen Jiongming died, his relatives held a funeral for him, but used the Zhi Gong Tang flag, indicating a different direction from the Nationalist Party. Who knew that the Zhi Gong Tang's ability to become a modern political party actually relied on the guidance of the pioneers of the Nationalist Party?

Autumn Day 326

— Jin Yi

In the deep autumn, in the early morning, in the silent world, there is the sound of leaves falling, the sunlight lingers only on the roof, the alley is still dark. This ancient city has not yet woken up, the shadow, four or five times larger than the main body, are intricately arranged on the ground, like the city's veins, but also dim. The autumn wind shakes people's bodies and also shakes people's hearts. The lake water seems to be still, bearing a heavy mood. Crows are flying, circling, their black feathers, without any luster, rustily thickening the disgust for them, but they seem to be intelligently, having witnessed all these years of rise and fall, calling out with a disappointed voice, calling out so.

But there are countless people living in this city, living; there are good fantasies and hopes. Looking at it from this side, this city should have no day of death, because everyone hides their talents in their hearts, and when they meet they only say: "What a refreshing autumn!"

Is autumn so refreshing? On the golden roof tiles, there are thin grasses gradually turning golden, when the wind comes, the copper bell at the corner rings lonely. In this ringing sound, it seems that many things are about to be confessed; but they are not understood by people, nor are they known by people, only when a team of camels walks past, the string of bells under their necks rings out an answer that is not understood by people. And then, following these camels on their long journey, crossing mountains, crossing water, walking to the endless desert.

The desolate bugle is blowing.

The autumn sky is high and blue, and even though the gorgeous red leaves are trying their best to decorate it, they cannot help people think that the good days are gone, just like an old man in his twilight years thinking about death, he can only recall the past with endless sighs. But isn't the past all distant? Fantasizing about the silk tree, I see leaves like bird feathers, fluttering and falling on the road.

The frost of the previous night can gradually become bright beads.

The street is still quiet, the hunched-over street cleaner, wearing red clothes, sweeps the fallen leaves on the road, moving forward with slow steps. A policeman's yawn is heard far away. The morning bell of the temple is floating leisurely in the air. A lonely middle-aged man wakes up at this time.

Lately, the time he wakes up is earlier and earlier every day; and in the evening, there is always greater fatigue pressing on him. Every day he is thinking! "This should have a long and good sleep"; but he often wakes up very early, and is anxious, wanting to catch back what has slipped away from him, but it only becomes impossible. In the past, he was surprised by this strange phenomenon, but gradually he understood, knowing that on the road of life he can already see the shadow of aging in the distant place.

Therefore, everything can be explained, that often sore body, that heavier melancholy, that fearful autumn scenery, that dark shadow that pounces on his heart, bigger and darker, ...

He sat up, put his feet into his shoes, dragged his lazy steps, and stood in front of the full-length mirror. Lately, he has been in the mood to look at himself every morning to see how much older he has become overnight. (To be continued)

Disappointment in Monetary Inflation, Gold Bar Price Rebounds and Rises 327

Bank of America Reduced Exchange Rates, Commodity Prices Plummeted, Market Opened Higher, One Yuan Exchange Speculation, Foreign Compensation, American Dollar Significantly Reduced, Final Result One Yuan Rises to Nine Yuan Sixty Cents

After the gold market broke through the 800 yuan mark, it seemed difficult to recover. Unexpectedly, yesterday the market rebounded again, rising significantly. Coinciding with the settlement, the final result was very firm. In the early morning, overseas silver markets in England and America both fell. The silver price on the Five Metals Exchange was reduced by four to five and a half cents. The exchange rate for England and America was reduced by 6.625 cents, America, England, and France plummeted by 13.75 cents and 24.5 cents. England and France also rose by one yuan. American cotton fell by 21 pounds, stocks fell by 3.49 yuan. American cotton was cheaper by five cents. London spot gold fell by 6.5 pence. The price of new American mined gold was 30.625 yuan, a decrease of 0.29 yuan from before. The gross opening price rose by nearly 30 yuan, to over 820 yuan. Then, due to the appearance of the Bank of China's November US dollar at 29.4375 yuan, it retreated to within 20 yuan. After the opening, due to the bank's continuous buying, the exchange market hardened, and the situation fluctuated and declined. However, because of the prior knowledge that the Hongkong and Shanghai Bank's listing was flat for British currency and the American dollar suddenly reduced by one yuan, people's confidence was boosted and it rebounded again. Finally, due to the continued efforts of fellow traders, the bank's buying slowed, the domestic market tightened, and the short covering momentum was strong. It then broke through the 20 yuan mark again. The afternoon closing was the most popular. The increase during the half-day was not small. Reuters reported that stock prices were under pressure because American speculation was shorting, due to the government's apparent abandonment of inflation, exchange rates and commodity prices rose and fell, and American citizens opposed the recovery measures. These news all had a significant impact. This settlement period, the listing was posted by the short side at 7.1 yuan, given a red price of 1,135 yuan. Now, the market conditions for the half-day are recorded as follows:

The opening price in the morning was 817.7 yuan, an increase of 23 yuan from the previous closing price. Commodity opening was 7.8 yuan. The exchange market opening price in the morning was a selling price of 1 shilling 3.375 pence for British currency and 29.25 yuan for American currency. Macquarie immediately bought, US dollar January 8.125 yuan. The situation was difficult to recover, and it decreased from 8.5 yuan. Trade Declining and Long-Term Loans Have Few Transactions - Due to Many Reasons... Let's See After the 20th - 330

All trades are declining, and cash is concentrated, resulting in the good long-term transaction, at this launching time, turning to silence, which is lamentable. The reporter inquired about the current long-term due date, which is approaching, and there must be some access. So he turned to key figures in the money industry to inquire about the situation. According to the answer, there are several reasons why it cannot be prosperous: (1) Since the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the vitality of various industries has declined and is difficult to recover, resulting in cash not being circulated after it is concentrated. (2) This year, most industries have more losses than profits, and the number of profitable industries is like a phoenix feather and unicorn horn. For the sake of cautious lending, they dare to be as lenient as possible. (3) The long-term loans due at the end of April, because the goods have not recovered, are cleared by owing this and owing that, and accumulated and pledged in turn, and there is no time to clear them. Therefore, the current term all want to urge collection, but how the market is like this, whether it can be repaid as desired is still unknown. (4) Ningbo's long-term loans, which were no less than tens of millions in previous years, after the recovery of some at the end of April, are now less than tens of millions, and there are many bad debts. It is feared that most of the current term will be transferred and only interest will be paid. It is difficult to seek recovery. As for new transactions, it is not possible to talk about them at the present time. We must wait until after the 20th to determine the action. Although the money houses currently have a lot of deposits, most of the excellent transactions have been seized by Chinese commercial banks, and they will not be able to do the more superior accounts. From the above observations, the situation of long-term access in the current term is feared to be far inferior to the situation at the end of April.

Silk and Tea - Overseas Silk Sales Show Increasing Weakness 348

(Shipping of Eight-Cocoon Eri Silk to the United States is Obstructed) The eight-cocoon eri silk (i.e., wild silk) produced in Shandong and the three northeastern provinces of China is a unique natural product, and its sales have historically relied on the United States as its main destination. Monthly exports amounted to several hundred bales. In recent years, the wild silk produced in Korea has flourished, greatly impacting the sales of eri silk to the United States. Coupled with the spread of labor strikes in the United States, the consumption of raw silk has drastically decreased, and the shipping of eri cocoons to the United States has become increasingly difficult. In the most recent month (September 10th to October 10th), only 155 bales of eight-cocoon eri silk were shipped to New York, San Francisco, Seattle, and other ports.

(Scarce Shipments of Jiaxing Green Silk to Shanghai) Jiaxing green silk is a unique product of China, historically sold to Europe and the United States. However, the production volume is not high, with only a few hundred bales exported annually. This year's cocoon production was not abundant, and shipments of green silk to Shanghai were scarce. In the most recent half-month, only 35 pieces were shipped.

(Increasingly Quiet Sales of Artificial Silk to Customers) The price of artificial silk in this port is trending upwards due to the tight exchange rate, and sales to customers are increasingly quiet. Only the Shanghai silk factories imported 22 cases of Feima, Jinyu, and Liuhai brands, with prices ranging from 178 yuan 9 jiao and 5 fen to 163 yuan 5 jiao net.

(Unusually Low Prices for European and American Telegraphic Transfer Silk) The foreign-managed silk market in this port has been in a state of decline. Overseas silk sales have been decreasing due to oversupply, and silk prices have been gradually decreasing. The telegraphic transfer price of white filature silk in New York is only 612 yuan, and in Lyon, it is only over 700 yuan (both B grade). The cost of each factory is between 760 to 770 yuan to 850 to 860 yuan, a difference of 150 to 160 yuan. The factories are incurring huge losses and cannot afford to dump their goods. The market is quiet. Yesterday, only Yin Zhuang and others imported 8 bales of yellow filature silk and 11 bales of yellow coarse silk, with prices remaining generally weak.

Yesterday, in the foreign-managed tea market of this port, English firms such as Jardine Matheson and Tongfu resumed purchasing high and medium-grade Keemun black tea due to receiving inquiries from England, and a total of 191 cases were traded for a price of 87 to 90 yuan. Trading in various green teas was scarce. Most of the high-grade Zhenmei teas from Tunxi and Shexian have already been sold out, and only residual goods remain on the market. Chinese merchants are maintaining a firm stance on price increases, and the trend in the tea market is stable.
